china didn't want us to know 
now its own file are do the talk 
by adrian zenz nov 24 2019 no more deny no more dodge 
the china communist party can no long hide its relentless campaign of mass internment against the ethnic minority in the northwestern region of xinjiang or claim that the effort is an innocuous educational program 
what was already widely known vastly report and confirmed by firsthand account has now been prove beyond doubt by the government's own record — gigabyte of file ream of report thousand of spreadsheet — some of them classified and highly confidential 
last weekend the new york times disclose and analyze the contents of a trove of leak internal china government document that outline specific policy for how to repress xinjiang's predominantly muslim minority — and reveal that president xi jinp himself set out the foundation for them 
this sunday the contents of two more set of document — all of which i have review — are being disclose 
among the first batch also leak is a confidential telegram sign by zhu hailun xinjiang's deputy party secretary which detail how local authority should manage and operate the vocational skill training center — a euphemism for the internment camp 
all translate here are mine 
the second set of document a large cache of file and spreadsheet from local government reveal the internment campaign's devastating economic and social impact on the family and community it target 
the telegram — dated nov 5 2017 and address to local politics and legal affair bureau — is marked extremely urgent and bear the secondhighest level of secrecy within china's classifieddocument scheme 
it reveal the extent of the security and surveillance measure taken around the camp partly to shield the camp from external scrutiny 
the message a directive note that the work conduct there is strict confidential and highly sensitive in nature 
even staff at the camp are forbidden from aggregate detainee figures 
the authorities' attempt to enforce absolute secrecy is confirmed by another document dated november 2018 this one from a local government file in hotan county 
it chide official for not protect secret related to the internment campaign well enough 
it stipulate that no person is under any circumstances permit to disseminate information about detention or reeducate via telephone smartphone or the internet and that official are strict forbidden from receiving related media interview or make unauthorized disclosure about the internment campaign 
that the china authority so deliberate sought to shield from external scrutiny information about operation at the xinjiang camp suggest that they are only too aware of how incriminate their policy and practice are 
i was also able to obtain a massive cache of local government file from within xinjiang 
among the most revealing document are thousand of detailed spreadsheet with the name identification numbers and address of ten of thousand of people mostly uighur and many of them in detention prison or reeducate camp 
in yarkand a county of about 800000 people in southwestern xinjiang 96 percent of the population is uighur 
six official spreadsheet about six village dated 2018 show that on average nearly 16 percent of the rural adult population was either interne or in prison 
in two village in kosherik township — which the document describe as heavy pollute by extremist ideology — nearly 60 percent of all household had one person or more interne 
in addition to the extraordinary scale of the internment campaign the file reveal its devastating impact well beyond the camp — deep into the community and family of xinjiang 
the spreadsheet show that the government has primarily target middleage men most often the head of the household and main wageearner 
beijing's occasional tour of its socall model camp often feature attractive young women 
in reality people between 30 and 59 were especially likely to be interne according to the spreadsheet 
the policy's socioeconomic fallout is dire — and local government are keeping a meticulous record of it 
one spreadsheet from 2017 for one town in yarkand county which list household with low income that might qualify for welfare included a young family with five children between the age of three and 14 
the father had been imprison the mother placed in a reeducate camp and the children in effect orphan 
in another hardly unusual case a household's two workingage parent were detain leave elderly grandparent — including a grandmother describe as seriously ill — to care for two toddler 
in a column with the header reason for poverty the relevant spreadsheet offer this explanation lack labor force and finances 
the toddlers' father isn't schedule to be release until 2030 
another spreadsheet from september 2018 show lists of loan default in pile township akto county 
in 80 percent of the case where the reason for default was list as internment most of the borrow funds were shown to still be in the bank 
a particularly depress example come from a village in yarkand county 
a uighur farmer and head of a family of five was interne in 2017 
in october 2016 he had received a loan of 40000 renminbi nearly 5700 to purchase agriculture machinery 
the equipment went unused during his detention — no other family member knew how to operate it — and the loan could not be repaid as schedule 
the government direct the family to rent out the equipment and send its oldest child a son to work 
the family was then officially marked as have been povertyalleviate by benefit from policy 
in june 2018 after his release the farmer applied for financial assistance so he could repay the loan and related interest 
in january 2019 he start to work in the yarkand county textile industrial park earn just 800 rmb about 113 a month 
by then the son age 20 had somehow become disabled and was list on government form as unable to work 
thanks to these new document disclosure we now have hard evidence — and the government's own evidence — that in addition to implement a vast internment program in xinjiang the china communist party is deliberate break up family and force them into poverty and a form of indenture labor 
for all its effort at secrecy the china government can no long hide the extent and the reach of its campaign of repression in xinjiang 
some important elements are still unknown 
the total internment figure remains a wellguarde secret 
base on the new evidence i have revise my own estimate i think that between 900000 and 18 million people have been detain in xinjiang since the spring of 2017 
also missing from the official document that have surface so far are precise record of how the detainee are treat and how exactly the process of reeducate works 
about those things however we have witness account 
the confidential telegram and local file do not mention the use of physical violence — but for one notable exception 
the telegram states that people who resist brainwashing must be single out for assaultstyle reeducate 
yet another sinister understatement and it suggest that force and torture may in fact be widely use 
in a way though we already know all that we really need to know 
the document that have been disclose these past few week reveal the staggering scale of the repression in xinjiang and its ruinous effects on the region's ethnic community well beyond the camp themselves 
consider this official statistics show that the combine net population growth rate of hotan and kashgar two of the largest uighur regions drop by about 84 percent between 2015 and 2018 
the china communist party set out it claim to transform through education ethnic minority in xinjiang 
in fact it is rip apart entire community and subjugate them on a colossal scale 
and this at the direction of president xi himself 
china's new civil religion by ian johnson dec 21 2019 beije — in the northern suburbs of this city is a small temple to a china folk deity lord guan a famous warrior deify more than a millennium ago 
renovate five years ago at the government's expense the temple is use by a group of retire who run pilgrimage to a holy mountain schoolchildren who come to learn traditional culture and a taoist priest who preach to wealthy urbanite about the traditional value of ancient china 
perch atop a hillock overlook the sprawl capital the temple is a microcosm of a new civil religion taking shape in china — an effort by the china communist party to satisfy china people's search for moral guidelines by supplement the largely irrelevant ideology of communism with a curate version of the past 
this new stateguide religios is the flip side of the government's harsh policy toward islam and christianity 
official believe these two global faith are hard to control because of their foreign tie and they have use negotiation or force — diplomacy with the vatican arrest of prominent protestant internment camp for muslim — to try to bring these religion to heel 
yet beijing's recent turn to tradition may be even more significant 
even though islam and christianity are world religion in china they remain minor with the number of their combine adherent amount to less than 10 percent of the population 
most china believe in an amalgam of buddhism taoism confucianism and other traditional value and idea that still resonate deep 
for this silent majority of hundred of million of people the government's newfound support for things like the temple to lord guan is welcome — a feeling that the china communist party hope will bolster its legitimacy especially given the irrelevance today of its found idea 
the benefit of its move to embrace the past may seem obvious but the shift mark a radical departure not just for a party officially committed to atheism but also from how reform over the past century have imagine a modern prosperous china 
from the 19th century onward china's elite argue that the country's tradition and faith were a major reason for its decline 
reform in 1898 call for temple to be convert into school 
while the nationalist party under chiang kaishek approve of four religion — buddhism taoism sometimes call dao christianity and islam — it largely considered traditional china belief to be superstition and advocate the destruction of temple 
scholar estimate that by the middle of the 20th century half of the temple that exist in china at the end of the 19th century had been destroy 
an 1851 survey of the old city of beije list 866 temple today i count just 18 
at the end of the 19th century most village had at least one temple and many had half a dozen vast section of the china countryside now have no temple at all 
when the communist took power in 1949 they like the nationalist officially recognize four religion — but then prompt began persecute them 
traditional faith came under especially harsh treatment with the government ban bedrock traditional practice from worship ancestor and local deity to following the advice of geomance master and spirit medium 
the three decade of reform that start in the late 1970s loosen control over society allow the revival of all religion and many tradition that had been proscribe 
despite periodic crackdown church and mosque but also temple were rebuilt and clergy train 
although all faith were supposed to remain under party control religious feeling boom with the number of believer in china topping 500 million by 2010 
xi jinping's rise to power in late 2012 mark a new era the third in the history of the china communist party's religious policy 
instead of the destruction of the mao years and the relatively laissezfaire approach of the reform period the state has embark on a form of highly curate revival 
one part of its approach rest on a deep suspicion of christianity and islam 
the party's policy toward islam has been the most draconian 
some believer especially uighur in the northwestern province of xinjiang have been subject to a policy of forced secularize 
this has included send hundred of thousand of muslim to reeducate camp compel restaurant to serve pork and alcohol and forbidding fast during ramadan 
the policy toward christianity is more nuance 
last year beije struck a deal with the vatican to joint appoint catholic bishop 
the vatican seem to hope to reverse the decline in the number of catholic in china 
but for beije the measure was a way to tighten control over the catholic clergy — and by extension the church itself 
protestant pose an especially vex problem for the party 
it is arguable china's fastestgrowe religion with an estimate 60 million or more adherent today compare with one million in 1949 including some 20 to 30 million who are thought to worship in unregistered or underground protestant church 
but the faith lack a unify structure that would allow for negotiation 
and so the government has fire a few shot across the bow close several of the country's bestknown underground church 
in many ways however the xi administration's embrace of traditional faith is more radical 
since taking office the president has met with buddhist leader and his government has allow taoism to flourish 
the state recently issue a landmark plan to improve social mores the first such program since 2001 
the plan stem from a widespread feeling that china's relentless drive to get ahead economically has create a spiritual vacuum and sometimes justify break rule and trample civility 
many people do not trust one another 
the government's blueprint for handle this moral crisis call for endorse certain traditional belief 
the epic paper — it runs to 10000 china character and would be significant long translate into english — doesn't mention communist china's found father mao zedong or his successor and their ideology focus instead on mr xi and his effort to fix social problem like money worship and hedonism 
it do invoke communist slogan such as core socialist value but in contrast to the previous such document from 2001 — which made only passing reference to china tradition — it call the past a rich source of morality 
the plan orders party official to promote ancient and worthy sage as well as to deep expound traditional concept such as ren'ai benevolence zhengyi righteous and jianyi zhengwei standing up brave for the truth 
this effort is not an attempt to replace communism with confucianism 
yet it is fair to say that for the first time since china's imperial order collapse in 1911 a central government is embrace the idea that made up the politicalreligious order that ran china for much of the past 2500 years 
why 
not only to address china's moral vacuum but also as a populist measure 
the country is enter a more uncertain era of slow growth and rising inequality and beije is drape itself in the mantle of tradition to broaden its appeal 
in do so the government seem to be assume that traditional china value and belief are easy to control than foreign religion and that support them will outweigh the costs of suppress islam and christianity 
but i have my doubt 
during a visit this fall to the lord guan temple i saw a dozen or so people mostly in their 30s and 40s reading works by wang yangm a philosopher born in the late 15th century 
on the face of it this was in line with government policy the party has embrace wang for exemplify an incorruptible spirit and matching words with deed 
but after reading a passage of wang's work the men and women sat around a big wooden table wield brush to write out over and over again his most famous phrase zhi xing he yi knowledge and action are one 
this knowledge according to wang come from an inner light a conscience — one that no government no matter how powerful can control

cuomo's bad medicine on medicaid by the editorial board jan 31 2020 for years new york state has operate one of the most generous medicaid program in the country a point of pride in a state with a long tradition of invest in the social safety net 
the program provide health care and other service to more than six million people largely lowincome new yorker and the costs are share between the state and federal government 
but profligate spend has sent costs spiral in recent years 
the medicaid program has become a driving force behind a 61 billion hole in new york's budget next year and a brew politics battle over what to do about it 
though medicaid costs are rising across the united states in new york — among the country's largest program and long one of its most expensive — spend has surge 
from 2015 to 2019 annual spend grew by an average of 6 percent according to a report last year by the empire center for public policy a conservative nonprofit research organization 
that's roughly double the rate of growth in the previous several years even as enrollment remain flat 
health care and budget expert have said a variety of factor are behind the trend including an increase in demand for personal care program that provide nonmedic service to disabled new yorker a minimumwage increase and financial assistance that the state has provided to struggle hospital 
new york's share of its 75 billion annual medicaid bill is now about 30 billion and grow imposing an increasingly untenable burden on state and local budget 
the federal government pay the rest 
the good news is that gov 
andrew cuomo who is in charge of administer the federal program has move to rein in costs 
the bad news is that he has said locality will have to pay for increase in local medicaid spend above 3 percent 
that's unfair and unrealistic 
local government in new york already pay more mandate medicaid costs than local government in any other state a dynamic that's been in place since the program began in the 1960s 
that's not unusual in new york where albany rely on new york city's tax base to fund the bulk of state service from education to commuter rails 
in 2018 local government in new york sent 76 billion to albany for the program according to a 2018 report from the citizen budget commission 
in fulton county in upstate new york for instance the local medicaid bill for 2016 amount to more than 15 percent of the county budget 
in new york city the annual medicaid tab is roughly 5 billion or nearly 5 percent of the city's budget 
if the spend increase continue and the state forces local government to pay for them the de blasio administration estimate the city would owe an additional 11 billion next year 
the state say the figure would be much lower 
mr cuomo has call on local government to reduce costs 
that's fine new york city and county across the state which oversee enrollment should work to root out any fraud or abuse and ensure that those who sign up for the program are eligible and truly in need 
they are the ontheground administrator 
we respond to them mr cuomo said in a phone call wednesday 
really though local government have limited say over how the program is run 
most of that responsibility rest with the state 
when it come to reduce medicaid costs that's where the focus should remain 
the most promising effort so far is mr cuomo's medicaid redesign team a working group assign to find 25 billion in savings this year preserve benefit while slash waste 
the governor use a similar task force to successful carry out costsave medicaid reform nearly a decade ago aid by the afford care act 
the new group will be led by the same two men michael dowl the president and ceo 
of northwell health and by dennis rivera the former head of 1199 seiu the powerhouse health care union 
they are set to make their recommendation ahead of the april 1 budget deadline 
it will be up to mr cuomo to ensure the public good is top of mind 
the redesign group should issue a thorough report present its finding to the public and the legislature 
right now it's not clear they plan to do so and that's a problem 
while not perfect the approach is far better than simply fork over more and more taxpayer dollar and stick local government with an evergrowe tab as the state has been do 
to get new york's medicaid program back on track the group will need to take a hard look at spend on nonmedic service like cooking and bathing for homebound new yorker 
according to the empire center new york's medicaid spend on such personal service was the highest in the country 
that may be because of a program that has expand in recent years in which medicaid pay nonmedic provider like family member to care for client 
in 2016 personal spend in new york account for 40 percent of national medicaid spend for the category overall up from 23 percent in 2011 the empire center said 
complicate matter is a politics dynamic friendly to the health care industry 
in 2018 for example the greater new york hospital association gave more than 1 million in politics contribution to the state's democratic party 
not long afterward the state increase medicaid reimbursement rate for the first time since 2008 cost the state an estimate 140 million per year 
mr cuomo has deny that donation influence his policy decision and cuomo administration official said at the time that the increase was necessary and simply long overdue 
health care expert disagree and say hospital revenue had already been on the rise 
new york's medicaid bill is out of control 
the first order of business is to understand more about why and to be honest with the public about what needs to be done about it

four key things you should know about health care by ezekiel j emanuel and victor r fuch sept 12 2019 health care so far perhaps the biggest issue in the democratic primary is also the most complicated issue facing government and the public 
unfortunately the debate is fill with persistent misconception from the role insurance company profit play in health care costs to who is actually pay for workers' health coverage 
clarify four fundamental health care fallacy could make it easy for voter to square some of the democratic proposal — and their critique — with reality fallacy no 
1 employer pay for employees' health insurance 
employer write check that cover most health insurance premium for employee and their dependent 
but as the princeton health economist uwe reinhardt once explain employersponsore insurance is like a pickpocket taking money out of your wallet at a bar and buy you a drink 
you appreciate the cocktail until you realize you paid for it yourself 
with health coverage employer write the check to the insurer but employee bear the cost of the premium — the entire premium not just the portion list as their contribution on their pay stub 
the premium money that go to the insurance company is cash that employer would otherwise deposit in employees' account like the rest of their salary 
the fallacy is in thinking an employer's contribution come out of profit 
in fact higher health insurance premium mean lower wages for worker 
since 1999 health insurance premium have increase 147 percent and employer profit have increase 148 percent 
but in that time average wages have hardly move increase just 7 percent 
clearly workers' wages not corporate profit have been pay for higher health insurance premium 
health care costs are one — though not the only — reason wages have stagnate over the last few decade 
with health insurance costs rising fast than growth in the economy more labor costs go to benefit like health insurance and less to takehome pay 
yet the belief that employee don't pay for their own health insurance is widespread 
one reason is that individual cannot be sure what cause their wages to change or remain stagnant for decade 
another reason is that employer want america to believe that they pay for their workers' health insurance 
still another reason is that there are those who profit from the employmentbase system drug company device manufacturer specialty physician and highincome individual 
they all want you to believe company are being magnanimous in give you insurance 
who else benefit from the belief in this fallacy 
opponent of national health insurance 
fallacy no 
2 medicare for all is unaffordable 
the key to evaluate the cost of medicare for all is to distinguish between increase spend on health care and shift expenditure from private insurance to the federal government 
true medicare for all would increase federal health care spend 
but that is not the same as increase total health care spend which was over 35 trillion last year 
instead medicare for all would move money from one column private health insurance spend to another federal health spend it do not automatic increase total costs 
a recent study by the mercatu center at george mason university — a freemarket center generally hostile to government program — estimate that for the 10 years between 2022 and 2031 the total national health costs for senator bernie sanders's medicare for all plan would actually be 501 trillion 
that would be 2 trillion less than if we let the system operate as it current do 
however mercatu research doubt that the sanders's plan would ultimately save trillion because they believe congress would have to increase medicare rate paid to hospital and physician to get the legislation enact 
they may be right — or wrong 
but that is a different argument — a prediction about the politics of enact law — than that medicare for all would inherently increase total health care spend 
we have our doubt about medicare for all 
but unaffordable is not a reason to oppose it 
whether it's our current arrangement or a future medicare for all the per capita cost of our health care system already far exceed that of any other industrialize country — including those with singlepayer system 
when you hear a health care price tag in the trillion know that the existing system has already brought us there 
fallacy no 
3 insurance companies' profit drive health care costs 
in the second democratic presidential debate senator bernie sander declared that the health care industry make 100 billion in profit 
he once rail against the insurance company anthem for deny a claim while note that it report fourthquarter profit for 2017 had increase by 234 percent to 12 billion 
many america believe that profit have no place in health care 
they see forprofit health insurance like buy and sell kidney and liver for transplant as what the nobel prize winner alvin roth term a repugnant industry — something that should not be exchange in the market 
that is an important moral stand but it make no difference to the claim that eliminate forprofit insurer will reduce high health care costs 
the fact is we could eliminate those profit and it would hardly matter to the cost of health care 
you would not notice it in your premium 
for the eight largest forprofit health insurance company in 2016 their cumulative revenue amount to nearly 4522 billion and profit were 221 billion for a profit margin of about 5 percent 
by contrast technology company bank and major drug company generally make more than 20 percent profit 
true 221 billion is a lot of money — but it is 06 percent of health spend 
and last year alone health care costs increase over 130 billion — six times insurance company profit 
health care spend would not be significant cheap if all insurance companies' profit were zero 
there are far more savings to be had in other effort — by cutting unnecessary patient service for example or by making physician and hospital more efficient — to deliver the same care at a lower cost 
fallacy no 
4 price transparency can bring down health care costs 
hospital will be require to publish price that reflect what people pay for service said president trump when he sign his executive order on health care price transparency 
price will come down by numbers that you wouldn't believe 
the cost of health care will go way way down 
there is no doubt that price for medical procedure can range widely even within the same city or state 
for instance mri of the spine can vary threefold in massachusetts and mammogram fivefold in san francisco 
conservative argue that inform patient of price for test and treatment will induce them to shop for lowercost service saving them insurer and the country money 
in theory the beauty of price transparency is that neither the government nor insurer impose cost control the invisible hand of the market do it all 
yet demonstration of price transparency have been try many times in many place and in reality it has not reduce the cost of care 
one recent study by harvard medical school research involved hundred of thousand of employee and use a website telling them what they would pay outofpocket if they chose particular physician and hospital 
the result no savings 
a followup study use another set of employer and another price transparency tool found the same result no savings 
since 2007 new hampshire has had a state website nh health cost that allow patient to select a medical procedure insurer and zip code and then get a list of price for the procedure from various provider 
the most promising study of nh health cost suggest a few million dollar in savings per year 
that works out to be about 5 per new hampshire resident 
the fact is price transparency will not make health care costs go way way down 
health insurance insulate the patient from price 
over 80 percent of the cost of medical care is paid by private and public insurance 
patient have little incentive to seek out the cheapest provider 
when price website exist few patient use them 
even in the most favorable study when offer a price transparency tool only 12 percent of patient took advantage of it usually it's less than 4 percent of patient 
furthermore price consideration are useful for choose only about 40 percent of procedure — routine service like colonoscopy mri 
scan and laboratory test 
most of the expensive service — think heart catheter cancer chemotherapy and organ transplant — are not the kind of thing you decide base on price 
finally in health care america usually put relationship ahead of money 
once patient find a physician they trust and a hospital they like they tend to stick with them even if there is a lowercost alternative nearby 
america health care is complex and any simplistic solution is likely to be base on a fallacy 
but that doesn't mean there is nothing we can do 
there are solution — they just don't make for bumper sticker phrase like medicare for all or eliminate forprofit insurer or price transparency

how much of harvard's 40 billion endowment is invest in fossil fuel 
by devi lockwood jan 29 2020 in my senior year at harvard i was invite to a dinner in honor of the writer margaret atwood the recipient of the 2014 harvard arts medal 
on my way out the door i linger shrug on my coat took a deep breath and walk up to the university's president at the time drew gilpin faust 
we had met twice once during her office hour and at an ice cream social 
please divest from fossil fuel i said hope to catch her off guard 
the president at first seemingly happy to see me rearrange her face 
her shoulder crept up toward her ear 
you student don't understand investment she said 
then she walk out of the room 
i have benefit immeasurable from harvard's investment in me 
but recognize where some of harvard's 40 billion endowment is invest was a cause of grow unease for me and some of my classmate 
student at other campus were similarly concerned about the endowment of their school 
figure out exactly how much of harvard's endowment is invest in oil gas and coal company is a nearimpossible task 
harvard is require to disclose only direct investment in which the university own shares of a specific company 
harvard say its direct investment amount to 394 million as of may 2019 or roughly 1 percent of the endowment total 
divest harvard a student group determined that of that approximate amount 56 million was invest in company that produce or own reserve of oil natural gas and coal and large electric utility power by natural gas and coal 
harvard doesn't comment on its individual investment 
but in 2015 the south pole group a carbon finance consultant in zurich analyze 989 million of harvard's then 364 billion endowment at the request of divest harvard and 350org 
base on those investment the group estimate that the overall endowment was responsible for annual emission of 11 million ton of carbon dioxide roughly equivalent to the annual emission from delaware 
it's easy to get bog down in the numbers but the exact amount of harvard's fossil fuel investment or the emission it is responsible for isn't all that important 
as the world face a climate crisis any amount of investment in company that extract or burn fossil fuel is too much especially by one of the world's leading university 
lawrence bacow the university's current president explain in the harvard gazette last fall that rather than divest the university believe that engaging with industry to confront the challenge of climate change is ultimately a sound and more effective approach for our university 
but many student have not been content with that approach 
as part of a divest campaign in may 2014 an undergraduate brett roche was arrest by harvard university police for block an entrance to massachusetts hall where president faust and member of the administration had their offices 
in april 2015 during harvard heat week student faculty alumni and community member blockade president faust's office once more 
last november at the harvardyale football game climate change protest storm the field at half time delay the game for roughly an hour 
to date 532 faculty member have sign a petition in favor of divest from fossil fuel 
the result 
nothing has happen 
other campus have had more luck 
after pressure from student group stanford announce in 2014 that it would not make direct investment in public trade company whose principal business is coal mining 
the university of maine follow suit in 2015 divest all direct holding from coal company 
in 2017 columbia university announce divest from producer of coal burn to generate electricity 
other school have taken additional steps divest not only from coal producer but also from oil and gas company 
these include sterling college in 2013 the university of hawaii university of dayton syracuse university and the rhode island school of design in 2015 and the university of oregon in 2016 
the university of california system announce last september that it would divest 13 billion of its 83 billion endowment and 70 billion of pension from fossil fuel producer 
recognize that student activism hasn't work on its own two harvard college alumni from the class of 2018 danielle strasburger and nath�n goldberg start thinking about the harvard board of overseer election 
last year they found harvard forward an alumnirun organization that aim to elect five recently graduate candidate to the board 
the board of overseer mostly advise the university on strategic decision though it do have the power to consent to the election of member to the harvard corporation 
the average age of the five candidate is 28 — the same number of years that on average have pass since the current overseer were harvard student 
their platform include complete and swift divest of all university asset from fossil fuel 
the board is compose of 30 harvard alumni who sit for sixyear terms 
each year in april five new member are vote in by alumni 
a nomination committee of the harvard alumni association generally choose eight candidate who will be add to the slate 
there's another way in though — though a petition process 
to qualify each candidate needs 2936 sign nomination form equivalent to 1 percent of eligible voter living harvard alumni with the exception of current professor administrator and staff 
the first test will come on feb 1 the deadline to qualify for the ballot 
when we spoke last week ms strasburger estimate that between 2300 and 2400 nomination form had already been sign in favor of each candidate 
they are nearly there 
this is not just about harvard 
and it's also not just about whether you think divest is a strategy that is worth pursue or whether it has an impact 
rather harvard forward is a model for building power by young people — of break the logjam within large institution and making change happen 
this approach is not new 
from 1985 to 1991 harvard and radcliffe alumniae against apartheid campaign for harvard to divest its stock in company operate in south africa 
the organization use the same nominatebypetition system to elect four member to the board including archbishop desmond tutu who state that he would return his honorary degree unless harvard divest entire from south africa 
by the 1980s harvard did 
younger alumni realize then that they need a seat at the decision making table to create change 
that is exactly what harvard forward is seek 
on jan 15 harvard global network night over 100 volunteer for harvard forward — many of them alumni from the 1960s '70s and '80s — attend 50 alumni event in 20 states and 20 country with petition in hand 
that night alone they gather over 1000 signature 
alumni can submit petition to nominate the younger slate of candidate until the deadline on saturday at 5 pm harvard forward has volunteer in 35 city to collect form at signature party this week 
a lot of people want to know how they can make an impact when it come to climate ms strasburger told me 
if you have a chance to influence a 40 billion endowment that's a pretty big deal

wash your hand by elisabeth rosenthal jan 28 2020 america are watch with alarm as a new coronaviru spread in china and case pop up in the united states 
they are barrage with information about what kind of mask are best to prevent viral spread 
student are hand out mask in seattle 
mask have run out in brazo county tex 
hang on 
i've work as an emergency room physician 
and as a new york times correspondent in china i cover the sar outbreak in 2002 and 2003 during which a novel coronaviru first detect in guangdong sicken more than 8000 people and kill more than 800 
my two children attend elementary school in beije throughout the outbreak 
here are my main takeaway from that experience for ordinary people on the ground 1 
wash your hand frequent 
2 
don't go to the office when you are sick 
don't send your kid to school or day care when they are ill either 
notice i didn't say anything about mask 
have a mask with you as a precaution make sense if you are in the midst of an outbreak as i was when out report in the field during those month 
but wearing it constant is another matter 
i don a mask when visiting hospital where sar patient had been house 
i wore it in the market where wild animal that were the suspect source of the outbreak were being butcher blood droplet flying 
i wore it in crowded enclose space that i couldn't avoid like airplane and train as i traveled to city involved in the outbreak like guangzhou and hong kong 
you never know if the guy cough and sneeze two row ahead of you is ill or just has an allergy 
but outdoors infection don't spread well through the air 
those photo of people walking down street in china wearing mask are dramatic but uninformed 
and remember if a mask has perchance intercept virus that would have otherwise end up in your body then the mask is contaminate 
so in theory to be protect maybe you should use a new one for each outing 
the simple mask are better than nothing but not all that effective since they don't seal well 
for anyone tempt to go out and buy the gold standard n95 respirator note that they are uncomfortable 
breathing is more work 
it's hard to talk to people 
on one long flight at the height of the outbreak on which my few fellow passenger were mostly epidemiologist try to solve the sar puzzle many of us including me wore our mask for the first couple of hour on the flight 
then the food and beverage cart came 
though virus spread through droplet in the air a big worry to me was always transmission via what doctor call fomite infect item 
a virus get on a surface — a shoe or a doorknob or a tissue for example 
you touch the surface and then next touch your face or rub your nose 
it's a great way to acquire illness 
so after walking in the animal market i remove my shoe careful and did not take them into the hotel room 
and of course i wash my hand immediately 
remember by all indication sar which kill about 10 percent of those infect was a deadly virus than the new coronaviru circulate now 
so keep things in perspective 
face with sar many foreigner chose to leave beije or at least to send their children back to the united states 
our family stay kid included 
we want them with us and didn't want them to miss school especially during what would be their final year in china 
but equally important in making the decision was that the risk of get sar on an airplane or in the airport seem greater than being smart and careful while stay put in beije 
and we were i stop taking my kid to indoor playground or crowded mall or delicious but dense packed neighborhood beije restaurant 
out of an abundance of caution we cancel a family vacation to cambodia — though my fear was less about catching sar on the flight than that one of the kid would have a fever from an ear infection upon our return at a border screening and would be stuck in a prolonged quarantine in china 
we instead took a vacation within china where we carry mask with us but didn't use them except on a short domestic flight 
in time during the sar outbreak the government shut down theater and school in beije as it is do now in many china city because these virus are more easily transmit in such crowded place 
but there was also a lot of irrational behavior enter a village on the way to a hike near the great wall our car was stop by local who had set up a roadblock to check the temperature of all passenger 
they use an oral thermometer that was only minimal clean after each use 
what a great way to spread a virus 
the international school of beije where my children were student was one of the few in the capital — perhaps the only one — that stay open throughout the sar outbreak though the class were empty since so many kid had departed to their home country 
it was a studied but brave move since a parent at the school had gotten sar at the very beginning of the outbreak on a flight back from hong kong 
she recover fine but it was close to home and family were scared 
the school institute a bunch of simple precautionary policy a stern note to parent remind them not to send a child to school who was sick and warning them that student would be screen for fever with ear thermometer at the school door 
there was no share of food at lunch 
the teacher led the kid in frequent hand washing throughout the day at classroom sink while singing a prolonged hand washing song to ensure they did more than a cursory pass under the faucet with water only 
if a family left beije and came back the child would have to stay at home for an extend period before return to class to make sure they hadn't caught sar elsewhere 
with those precaution in place i observe something of a public health miracle not only did no child get sar but it seem no student was sick with anything at all for month on end 
no stomach bug 
no common cold 
attendance was more or less perfect 
the world health organization declared the sar outbreak contained in july 2003 
but oh that those habit persist 
the best firstline defense against sar or the new coronaviru or most any virus at all are the one that grandma and common sense taught us after all

no team trump the coronaviru isn't good for america by paul krugman jan 30 2020 how frightened should you be about the coronaviru 
i'm no epidemiologist but what i've seen looks pretty scary 
it doesn't help that the trump administration as part of its general war against science and expertise has seriously reduce america's capacity to respond if we do face a dangerous pandemic 
it also looks quite possible that the virus will inflict a lot of economic damage — even if it doesn't kill you it might kill your job 
and one special source of concern is that top official in the trump administration are talk nonsense about the economic threat 
so about that economic threat many people are drawing parallel between the coronaviru and the 20023 outbreak of severe acute respiratory syndrome or sar which also originate in china 
like the current outbreak sar led to the imposition of economically disrupt quarantine which appear to have had a significant if temporary adverse effect on china's economy and a modest negative impact on the world economy as a whole 
we still don't know whether the coronaviru is more or less dangerous than sar 
what we do know is that the global economic implication of a pandemic in china are likely to be much more severe now than they were then for the simple reason that china is a vastly big player than it use to be 
in 2002 china was still in the early stage of its great economic surge it account for only around 8 percent of global manufacture value add far less than the shares of the us japan and europe 
today however china is the workshop of the world account for more than a quarter of global manufacture 
now you might think that this imply an upside to china's trouble that disrupt china's vast manufacture sector would offer opportunity to producer in other country including the united states 
that is you might think this if you knew nothing about 21stcentury economics 
sure enough wilbur ross the commerce secretary appear on fox business on thursday morning to declare that he didn't want to talk about a victory lap but that the coronaviru will help to accelerate the return of job to north america 
by saying this he demonstrate a couple of things 1 why gail collins's reader vote him trump's worst cabinet member and 2 why trump's trade war has been such a failure 
what ross and his colleague apparently still don't understand — although some of them may be get an inkling — is that modern manufacture isn't like manufacture a couple of generation ago when different countries' industrial sector were engaged in fairly straightforward headtohead competition 
these days we live in a world of global value chain in which much of what any given nation import consist not of consumer goods but of intermediate goods that it use as part of its own production process 
in such a world anything that disrupt import — whether it's tariff or a virus — raise production costs and as a result if anything hurt manufacture 
indeed a recent study by the federal reserve found that trump's tariff which were concentrated on intermediate goods have reduce not increase manufacture output and employment 
sure enough while overall economic growth in 2019 was decent not great manufacture is in a recession 
and the uncertainty create by the trade war may explain why business investment is down despite a huge cut in corporate tax 
as i said some of trump's people seem to have gotten an inkling here 
last week the white house basically admitted that tariff on steel and aluminum have done more harm than good hurt industry that use these material 
but the administration's answer isn't a reconsider of its policy — it is to impose more tariff on a wide range of product 
which bring me back to the coronaviru 
let's leave aside the public health issue — although the trump administration has clearly left us much less prepared than we had been to deal with these issue if they become serious — and focus on the economics 
what we can say is that if the virus seriously disrupt china production its impact on the us economy will be like an extreme version of trump's trade war except without any compensation in the form of tariff revenue 
and the two things we know about the trade war are that it has been an economic bust and that trump's official still appear clueless about why it has been a bust 
bear in mind that so far trump has been remarkably lucky 
aside from hurricane maria — which he mishandle and in which thousand of america die — he has face essentially no crisis domestic or foreign that weren't of his own making 
and he has surround himself with the gang that couldn't think straight which raise severe doubt about how well he would handle a crisis that he didn't create himself 
if wilbur ross's bonehead remark on thursday are any indication — and i fear they are — the trump administration is even less prepared to deal with the economic fallout from a possible pandemic than it is to deal with the public health crisis 
be afraid 
notorious djt

tech lose a prophet 
just when it needs one 
by kara swish jan 29 2020 it's nothing but noise all the time 
we get hammer every second from an incessant sousaphone of tweet and from the righteous rage machine that scream at us in this digitize 247365 communications world that we have built 
what you might not know is that we have long had a name for what start this all disrupt innovation 
the concept was pioneer by clay christensen a highprofile and wellregarde harvard professor of management who die of cancer last week at 67 
professor christensen's remarkable legacy grew out of a seminal book he publish in 1997 the innovator's dilemma 
the book cover esoteric industry like the disk drive market and excavate to analyze and illustrate the power of disrupt technology 
his idea exploded through the thennascent internet scene and throughout silicon valley 
i recall reading an early copy and thinking that it was a manifesto that the tech world would embrace — and that professor christensen was tech's prophet 
the intel founder and chief executive andy grove was a fan 
so was the apple legend steve job 
both men were doubtless attract to the idea that startup made up of outsider could find ways to create new market and new value — and disrupt and overwhelm establish company 
in the face of disrupt old company could do almost nothing 
it wasn't that they couldn't see the new threat of startup but that they were stuck on serving their current business and they fail to change their product and service out of fear of cutting into profit 
professor christensen's formula was elegant first disrupt product are simple and cheap they generally promise lower margin not greater profit 
second disrupt technology typically are first commercialize in emerge or insignificant market 
and third leading firms' most profitable customer generally don't want and indeed initially can't use product base on disrupt technology 
it was that simple 
professor christensen's book came out a year before google was found seven years before facebook eight years before youtube and 11 years before uber 
each of these company knowingly or unknowing would follow his map 
while professor christensen would go on to write a sequel and many more books on adjacent topic ripe for disrupt like education disrupt class in 2008 and health care innovator's prescription in 2009 it was his initial idea that was devastating insightful 
i use the term devastate because though no fault of professor christensen's disrupt innovation took a turn for the worse in tech 
silicon valley fail to marry disrupt with a concept of corporate responsibility and growth at all costs became its motto 
the more measured approach that professor christensen taught was ignore 
thus in tech the idea was more like destructive innovation which to me was distill in facebook's famous sign that was once plastered all over the wall at its headquarters move fast and break things 
i have always wonder why the company chose those words 
i have no problem with move fast which professor christensen would not have quibble with since being nimble was a core competent that he tout 
it was the word break that stuck in my head like a bad migraine 
why use a violent and thoughtless word like break and not one more hopeful like change or transform or invent 
and if break was to be the choice what would happen after the break 
would there be fix 
could there be any fix after the break 
break sound painful 
and back to today's subject professor christensen never talk about that 
in fact professor christensen's approach was quite the opposite 
he learned in 2010 that he had lymphoma then he had a stroke 
within two years he publish the book that i like best titled how will you measure your life 
it is at turn spiritual and sometimes selfhelpy taking professor christensen's management thinking and apply it to how to live a life 
this book should be newly relevant as tech is casting about for its next act we've been talk about the negative impact of tech's disrupt innovation for a while now 
techy measure everything — and so professor christensen's bracing prescription are perhaps perfect as the tech industry seek redemption 
for example he wrote it's easy to hold your principles 100 percent of the time than it is to hold them 98 percent of the time

to defend their high price medical center assert that they couldn't afford to operate on medicare payment which are generally lower than what private insurer pay 
but the argument isn't convincing 
the cost of a hospital stay in the united states average 5220 a day in 2015 — and could be as high as over 17000 compare with 765 in australia

most economist think hospital could do just fine with far less than they get today from private insurance

pay buy the newest scanner whether it is need or not or install spa and zen garden

the bernie sander fallacy by david brook jan 16 2020 this is a golden age for they 
this is the belief that there is some malevolent elite they out there and they are destroy life for the rest of us

and there is bernie sanders's classwar they the billionaire have rig the economy to benefit themselves and impoverish everyone else 
each of these story take a genuine tension in society and blow it up into an allexplaine cartoon in which one part of america is try to destroy the other part 
the gop 
has been swallow by trump's culture war and many democrat seem to be rush to join sanders's class war 
these democrat are do this even though it's politics suicide 
classwar progressiv always lose to culturewar conservatism because swing voter in the midwest care more about their value — gun patriotism ending abortion masculinity whatever — than they do about proletarian class consciousness 
democrat are do this even though the sander classwar story is wrong 
sander start with a truth worker need more bargain power as they negotiate wages with their employer 
but then he blow this up into an allexplaine ideology capitalism is a system of exploit in which capitalist power completely dominate worker power 
this ideology crash against the fact 
in the first place over the past few years wages for worker toward the bottom of the income stream have been rising fast than wages for those toward the top 
if the boss have the worker by the throat how can this be happening 
second wages are still generally determined by skill and productivity 
for example edward lazear of stanford university find that between 1989 and 2017 productivity in mostly highskill industry rose by roughly 34 percent and wages in those industry rose by 26 percent 
productivity in industry with mostly lessskill worker rose by 20 percent while wages grew by 24 percent 
as michael strain of the america enterprise institute put it capitalism is do what it's supposed to do 
it's rewarding productivity with pay and some people and company are more productive 
if you improve worker bargain power that may help a bit but over the long run people can't earn what they don't produce 
third and most important most of the increase in earnings inequality has happen between company not within them 
as john van reenen of mit 
has found all over the world superstar business are racing ahead of their competitor 
as those company grow more productive they earn more profit per employee and pay their worker more 
company that can't match that productivity don't and their worker lag behind 
a recent brook institutionchumir foundation report also note that there is a grow productivity gap between superstar company and everybody else 
whether it is in tech retail manufacture utility or service productivity growth at the leading company in each industry has remain very strong 
those productive business are capture large and large market shares 
but productivity is not grow fast among the lagging company 
worker in those business suffer 
today's successful boss are do what they should be do increase productivity grow their business and offering great service 
a side effect of their efficiency is they spend a small share of their revenue on labor even while raise their workers' wages 
in a global informationage economy the rewards for being best are huge 
thus the core problem is not capitalist exploit their worker it's the rise of productivity inequality 
it's the company and individual who don't have the skill to take advantage of new technology 
the real solution therefore is not class war to hammer successful business 
it's to boost and expand productivity for everybody else 
that's done the oldfashione way — by have better school and better vocational training by have more open competitive market by create incentive to expand investment by making sure superstar business don't use lobbyist to lock in their advantage 
i understand if you want to stick to an usversusthem politics ideology 
it's emotionally satisfying to base your politics ideology on blame people you dislike 
in fact i strong recommend michael lind's new book the new class war which is the best version of usthem 
lind make a lot of vague generalization about the managerial elite which he blame for our problem 
but at least he's interesting and provocative 
at least he understand that a politics plausible they is economically left and social right — combine the culture war and class war into a tidy narrative 
but if you want to deal with our real problem stop the usthem warfare and start dealing with productivity inequality 
successful executive are do what's best for their company gathering as much talent as they can 
this isn't evil 
it's not exploit 
the job of public policy is to make it easy for everybody to do what successful people are do 
productivity is the key to national prosperity 
every time we increase productivity for one person we all thrive a little more together

the meaningless of the org domain by sam wineburg and nadav ziv dec 5 2019 are today's high school student the one we call digital native able to separate fact from fiction

but 96 percent of student never uncover this industry connection 
too often students' evaluate stall at three letters this page is a reliable source to obtain information from one wrote you see in the url that it end in org as oppose to com 
the kid are wrong 
dotorg symbolize neither quality nor trustworthy 
it's a marketing tool that rely on a widespread but false association with credibility 
kid aren't the only one misinform 
a 2012 international study found that nearly half of america and large percentage in france brazil and india believe that an organization must meet some criteria before it could register under org 
the dotorg domain is control by the public interest registry which was sold last month to ethos capital a private equity firm 
the three letters are market as a powerful signal that your site serve a greater good — rather than just a bottom line 
it's a claim that leads people to make error about whom and what to trust 
unlike dotgov or dotedu which are closed to the general public dotorg is an open domain 
anyone can register a dotorg without passing a character test 
even commercial site can be dotorg 
craigslist — among the world's largest ad site — is craigslistorg 
there are over 10 million dotorg each of which pay roughly 10 per year to register 
all you have to do to get one is fill out an online form and provide payment 
registration fee generate 92 million in revenue for the public interest registry in 2018 alone 
in theory these revenue could grow much large soon — in june the internet corporation for assign name and numbers the supervisory body that regulate the internet's domain name system agree to lift price cap on dotorg 
still andy shea a spokesperson for the public interest registry say it plan to keep the price for dotorg low with increase of no more than 10 percent on average a year 
in the public interest registry's latest marketing blitz they unveil a logo paint in deep royal blue a shade they say evoke feelings of trust security and reliability 
they tell new customer to expect an increase in donation and trust for donor when they become part of the domain of trust 
noteworthy nonprofit civic organization and religious group have embrace the domain — and so have a host of bad actor 
all reap the benefit of dotorg's association with credibility 
educational institution unwitting shape misperception around dotorg 
many college and university including harvard and northwestern steer student in the wrong direction 
they equate dotorg with nonprofit group and issue no warning of the danger lurk beneath the domain's positive aura 
dotorg is the favored designation of astroturf site group that masquerade as grass roots effort but are back by corporate and politics interests 
one of these is the employment policy institute which claim to sponsor nonpartisan research 
it was actually found and run by the head of a public relations firm that represent the restaurant industry 
another dotorg america for prosperity foundation say it address major social problem through broadbase grass roots outreach 
in reality it was found by the billionaire koch brother and many of its grass roots activist are paid 
there's an even big risk to equate dotorg site with dogooder 
dozen of neonazi antilgbt antimuslim and antiimmigrant group bear the dotorg seal 
a random sample of a hundred organization designate as hate group by the southern poverty law center found that 49 percent carry the dotorg domain 
typically the domain name system is not an appropriate tool to address website content question and speech issue said shea the public interest registry spokesperson 
that said if a site on a org domain engage in specific threat of violence we would not hesitate to take action on it under our antiabuse policy 
a 2019 united nation survey show that citizen the world over have lost trust in the internet 
restore it will take herculean effort 
the group that control the internet's domain system could lead the way by being honest about what these initial do and don't represent 
the public interest registry and ethos capital could channel some of the million earn from the dotorg mirage to fund initiative that educate the public on the domain's shortcoming 
they can start by add a bright red asterisk to their royal blue logo dotorg imply nothing about an organization's intent 
buyer beware

of civil society with big national voice and large decentralize national organization so that people across america had easy and practical pathway to get involved in community revival

in the 2020s that feeling vanish

america were more collaborate in the 2020s 
and the new york met won the world series every single year 
the shaky future of org domain by josephine wolff jan 27 2020 online commerce and forprofit activity have largely shaped the internet over the past 25 years but a few important corner of the internet have remain staunch nonprofit retain some of the internet's early charm and resistance to commercial interests 
one of those corner is the org toplevel domain the goto domain for nonprofit and nongovernmental organization look to establish an afford and reputable online presence 
domain name for website like nytimescom or unorg or tuftsedu are the key real estate of the internet 
without a domain it is next to impossible to have an online presence there are now more than 350 million domain name register worldwide 
those domain name are sold to customer by registrar like godaddy which partner with registry like verisign which manage the com toplevel domain or all the domain name ending in com 
domain name are big business — there's a lot of money at stake when divvy them up among all the registrar and registry 
at the top of the domain name hierarchy sit the internet corporation for assign name and numbers a nonprofit that designate which registry control which toplevel domain and help resolve dispute around domain ownership 
icann has a unique governance structure it is run by a board of director that incorporate feedback from different advisory committee compose of government official industry representative and civil society member 
it is a model that icann refer to as multistakeholder governance base on the premise that all user of the internet deserve a say in how it is run 
since 2002 domain ending in org have been purchase through an agency call the public interest registry which is own by the internet society a wellregarde nonprofit working to expand access to the internet across the world 
but in november the internet society announce it was plan to sell the public interest registry — along with control of all the org domain — for 11 billion to a recently form private equity company call ethos capital with close tie to former leader of the internet governance community 
the propose sale has spark outrage from many people at prominent internet nonprofit including the wikimedia foundation and the electronic frontier foundation and rightly so 
one worry is that ethos in an attempt to make the org toplevel domain as profitable as possible will rapid raise price for its customer 
for years a 2013 contract cap the cost of an org domain at 825 with an allow increase of no more than 10 percent a year — a restriction that kept org domain afford 
today a org domain costs 993 a year 
but in june 2019 icann approve a new contract with the public interest registry eliminate the price cap even though thousand of people voice opposition to that decision during a period of public comment 
ethos has said it will continue to raise price for org domain by no more than 10 percent per year but it's not clear how those promise will be enforce or by whom and the timing of the sale — following immediately on the eliminate of the price cap — has contribute to some of the skepticism surrounding the deal 
another fear is that ethos will cave to pressure from foreign government about which organization should and should not be allow to own org domain 
current org is an open domain so anyone is allow to register a org domain and there are more than 10 million of them register worldwide 
but the public internet registry has the authority to suspend domain name for illegal activity and one of the concern raise in a public letter oppose the sale is the potential for government to target ngo by accuse them of illegal activity and pressure the public internet registry to take down their domain 
just last month for instance the china government sanction five united statesheadquartere ngo for their involve in the protest in hong kong all five of those ngo have org domain 
there are other reason to be worried about the sale 
the circumstances of the deal between ethos and the internet society seem at odds with the multistakeholder model of cooperative transparent governance that the internet community has work so hard to develop 
beyond just threaten the integrity of the org toplevel domain the sale of the public interest registry without any further community involve or oversight from icann threaten the integrity of that governance model and the public's trust that the organization responsible for running the internet have their best interests at heart 
icann has the ability to block the deal as well as to question the involved party about how they would manage the org domain and protect customer but in a statement to the financial times icann said it do not have authority over the propose acquisition a claim that is patently false 
icann itself in a blog post last month acknowledge that pir must obtain icann's prior approval before any transaction that would result in a change of control of the registry operator and pledge to take its responsibility in evaluate this propose transaction very seriously 
but while icann say it has ask pir for more information about the sale it has told the public very little about those inquiry or the ensue response and it has not solicit any public comment on the transaction 
icann's reasoning seem to be that since the sale do not threaten the security reliability or stability of the org domain it is not its place to intervene 
but icann regularly make decision about domain ownership that are unrelated to issue of security and stability — just last year for instance it grant amazon ownership of the amazon toplevel domain over the objection of several south america country 
that decision resolve a sevenyearlong dispute date to 2011 when icann decided to open up more toplevel domain beyond the standard one like com org and gov 
icann received nearly 2000 application in 2012 for new toplevel domain like google love microsoft and wine and for each application the applicant had to pay icann 185000 in addition to ongoing fee for maintain the domain 
this brought a massive influx of cash for icann that help fund its subsequent international expansion and the process of sever its final tie with the united states government in 2016 
the point of sever those tie was to engender greater international trust in icann and by extension the system of global internet governance that it oversee 
but instead icann seem at risk of being capture by commercial interests — a risk that first became apparent with the lucrative 2012 expansion of the toplevel domain that benefit no one besides icann 
odds are that seven years later you've still never interact with a website ending in one of those domain and if you have it was probably only a means of deliver spam or malware to your computer 
today icann is in a very delicate position because it derive its authority not from a contract with the united states but instead from its ability to balance the interests of all its various stakeholder from government official to civil society group and forprofit company and maintain credibility with the worldwide community 
it's easy to see why it is not eager to jump into the fray and interfere with or even question the ethos deal for fear of drawing criticism 
but the real risk to icann is in failing to protect the remain corner of the internet preserve for public good and letting its forprofit stakeholder become the dominant voice in its decisionmake process 
just as icann's former relationship with the united states government prove problematic for it in try to sustain a credible role in global governance activity so will a tooclose relationship with the forprofit sector at the expense of individual internet user 
icann should public investigate this sale so that all of its stakeholder can see exactly which safeguard will be put in place to protect org customer 
and if those safeguard are not sufficient or enforce if they meet with widespread disapproval and dissatisfaction from org customer and registrar then icann should make good on its promise to provide consensusbase multistakeholder governance and if necessary block the deal from go through 
icann cannot and should not be hiding from controversial domain dispute 
it is the only entity with authority over these decision and its willing to exercise that power will ultimately be good not just for the internet and internet user but also for icann itself

the three crucial flaw in trump's 'peace vision' by micah goodman jan 29 2020 president trump's “ultimate deal for israelipalestinian peace isn't ultimate and it isn't quite a deal 
release on tuesday the plan — or “peace vision as it's call in its official document — has three flaw 
none are fatal 
first the dissonance between its pretension and its timing it purport to change history but coming just one month before israel's election it serve petty politics 
second there is a mismatch between the plan's state aim and the actor who are meant to put it into place it seek to bring peace between israel and the palestinian but the palestinian are not full partner in its implement 
third and the biggest problem the plan doesn't meet the palestinians' minimum conditions 
can anyone imagine that the palestinian who have previous reject plan that offer them nearly 100 percent of the west bank might be happy with just 70 percent 
the peace plan in other words will not bring peace 
but these three flaw should not distract us from the big opportunity the plan presents it clever redivide even temporary the territory in dispute 
this division can rearrange the conflict 
if put in place the plan would create a palestinian state with almost full sovereignty on some 70 percent of the west bank while fully address israel's security needs 
the conflict would not end but it would be functional different 
the israelipalestinian conflict is a conflict between occupier and the occupy 
but after the plan it would become a conflict between two separate politics entity — and that's an entire new paradigm 
this should be the plan's big ambition instead of seek to end the battle it should fundamentally redraw the battle lines 
the problem with the “ultimate deal is the mismatch between the plan and its state aim 
as a peace plan it's laughable 
but sometimes all that's need to fix a problem is to rethink the purpose of the solution 
and here we can stop pretend that the united states plan will end the conflict and admit that it might be better at transform its character 
and with more modest goal it might enjoy better success 
to turn the trump administration's proposal from a bad plan to end the conflict into a good plan to transform the conflict all reference to ending the conflict should be remove 
the palestinian cannot be expect to recognize israel as a jewish state formal renounce the right of return or sign a document announce an “end to claim 
what would israel gain from a plan to reconfigure the conflict 
plenty 
most israel are trap between two national aspiration 
on the one hand they don't want to rule over the palestinian people but on the other they don't want to live under the threat of rocket from a palestinian state 
the tension between these two impulse has paralyze israel's ability to address the conflict 
a plan to reconfigure the conflict would dramatic reduce israel's control over the palestinian and do so without putt israel in danger 
in other words for israel the trump plan would smash the zerosum game between security and ending the occupation 
israel would be able to greatly reduce their rule over the palestinian without being any more threaten by them 
and what do the palestinian stand to gain from a plan to reconfigure the conflict 
also plenty 
the palestinian too are trap 
on the one hand they want an independent state of their own but on the other most of them want the palestinian refugee to “return — that is to be relocate to israel 
moreover a large section of palestinian society is unwill to recognize nonmuslim sovereignty over any part of the holy land 
reconcile with israel would be a religious concession and relinquish the “right of return would be a national concession 
for many palestinian those two concession would mean renounce their most sacred belief which form a part of palestinian identity 
for many years the various peace plan propose to the palestinian expect them to forgo these two axiom 
but the palestinian have always refuse a deal in which they would have to relinquish core elements of their national identity as the price for independence 
a plan to rearrange the conflict would give the palestinian a state without expect them to pay for it by renounce their demand for a right of return and thereby concede a plank of their national identity 
under the plan the new palestinian state will not be completely sovereign but it will be mostly sovereign and the elements of the occupation that immiserate palestinian in their daytoday lives — namely restriction on movement construction and economic growth — will be swept away 
in other words any plan would need to drop the pretense of realize either side's perfect deal 
this plan begin to do that 
under it the palestinian could dramatic enhance their sovereignty without concede their aspiration and israel should control far few palestinian without concede its security 
neither side will give up on what is truly important to it and both will reduce what is truly painful 
it won't be peace 
it won't be a new middle east 
but it will be progress 
conflict between neighbor are not only healthy than conflict between occupier and the occupy — they are also more likely to support negotiation 
talks in the future would be between two sovereign states 
in other words reconfigure the conflict will create new opportunity to continue shrink it 
it's time to stop devote our energy and politics capital to ending the conflict in a single “ultimate deal and start focus on a much more modest mission — transform its nature 
instead of reject the plan — we should think again about what it can and should realistic achieve 
that's the way to break through the deadlock minimize suffering and forge a new reality
