the wisdom your body know by david brook nov 28 2019 this has been a golden age for brain research 
we now have amazing brain scan that show which network in the brain ramp up during different activity 
but this emphasis on the brain has subtle fed the illusion that thinking happen only from the neck up 
it's fed the illusion that the advanced parts of our thinking are the rational parts up top that try to control the more primitive parts down below 
so it's interesting how many scientist are now focus on the thinking that happen not in your brain but in your gut 
you have neuron spread through your innards and there's increase attention on the vagu nerve which emerge from the brain stem and wander across the heart lung kidney and gut 
the vagu nerve is one of the pathway through which the body and brain talk to each other in an unconscious conversation 
much of this conversation is about how we are relate to other 
human thinking is not primarily about individual calculation but about social engagement and cooperation 
one of the leader in this field is stephen w porge of indiana university 
when you enter a new situation porge argue your body react 
your heart rate may go up 
your blood pressure may change 
signal go up to the brain which record the autonomy state you are in 
maybe you walk into a social situation that feel welcome 
green light 
your brain and body get prepared for a friendly conversation 
but maybe the person in front of you feel threaten 
yellow light 
you go into fightorflight mode 
your body instantly change 
your ear for example adjust to hear high and low frequency — a scream or a growl — rather than midrange frequency human speech 
or maybe the threat feel like a matter of life and death 
red light 
your brain and body begin to shut down 
according to porges's polyvagal theory the concept of safety is fundamental to our mental state 
people who have experienced trauma have body that are highly reactive to perceive threat 
they don't like public place with loud noise 
they live in fightorflight mode stress and anxious 
or if they feel trap and constrained they go numb 
their voice and tone go flat 
physical reaction shape our way of seeing and being 
lisa feldman barrett of northeastern university also argue that a main purpose of the brain is to read the body and to regulate what she call the body budget 
you may see a bully on the playground 
your brain then predict your next action and speed your heart rate and breathing to deal with it 
you experience these change as emotion — oh this is fear or oh this is anger — because your brain has create an emotion concept to make those physical change meaningful 
you might think that in everyday life the things you see and hear influence what you feel but it's mostly the other way around what you feel alter your sight and hearing barrett write in how emotion are made 
when we're really young we know few emotion concept 
young children say mommy i hate you 
when they mean i don't like this because they haven't learned their culture's concept for hatred vs bad 
but as we get old we learn more emotional granular 
the emotionally wise person can create distinct experience of disappointment anger spite resentment grouchy and aggravation whereas for a less emotionally wise person those are all synonym for i feel bad 
a wise person may know the foreign words that express emotion we can't name in english tocka russia roughly for spiritual anguish or litost czech roughly for misery combine with the hunger for revenge 
people with high emotional granular respond flexible to life have better mental health outcome and drink less 
if bodily reaction can drive people apart they can also heal 
martha g welch of columbia university points to the importance of loving physical touch especially in the first 1000 minutes of life to lay down marker of emotional stability 
under the old brainon paradigm welch argue we told people to selfregulate their emotion through conscious selftalk 
but real emotional help come through coregulation 
when a mother and a child physically hold each other their bodily autonomy states harmonize connect on a metabolic level 
together they move from separate distress to mutual calm 
welch has create something call the welch emotional connection screen which measure the emotional connection between mother and preterm baby 
by encourage this kind of deep visceral connection through 18 month her therapy can mitigate the effects of autism 
when you step back and see the brain and body thinking together the old distinction between reason and emotion doesn't seem to make sense 
your very perception of the world is shaped by the prediction your brain is making about your physical autonomy states 
you also see how important it is to teach emotional granular something our culture pay almost no attention to 
you also see that we're not separate brains cool observing each other 
we're physical viscera deep interact with each other 
the important communication is happening at a much deep level

put another way tribe continue my right not to be upset by your appearance or life choice cannot occupy the same plane as your right to live your life as you opt to or are compel to live it if we are to have a viable social and legal system 
one needn't be a libertarian to recognize that there is a difference in kind between someone's genuine right to be free of another's physical intrusion or displacement and someone's ersatz right to be free of another's merely offend or upset behavior or circumstances 
in this view according to tribe rights of the first or primary sort can be universally recognize rights of the second sort must be subordinate if social life is to be tolerable

we hate data collection 
that doesn't mean we can stop it 
by farhad manjoo nov 15 2019 we're being watch 
we know we're being watch and we don't think the watch have our best interests at heart 
they try to mollify us argue that we're being watch for our own good and that in fact we're the one in charge of the scale and scope of all the watch but deep down most of us are confuse and suspicious about this sudden state of affair 
why are they watch us so close 
what will they do with all they learn about us 
is there any hope of stopping them 
and do it even matter that we do not want to be watch — or is it of no consequence because they know we're trap and so do we 
the above may sound like the ravings of a wretch imprison in the panopticon but according to a survey of more than 4000 people conduct this summer by the pew research center it is the widespread sensibility of the day 
according to the survey america in 2019 feel adrift and powerless about living under the glare of digital surveillance 
twothird of america believe that surveillance is an inevitable consequence of modern existence — it is not possible to go through daily life they say without company and the government collect data about them 
more than 70 percent believe that most or all of what they do online is being track and nearly that many believe the same is true of what they do offline 
and more than 80 percent feel like they have very little or no control over the data being collected about them 
in some ways the numbers are unsurprise of course people who are being watch all the time feel that they're being watch all the time 
yet the survey also suggest a major failing on the part of corporation and the government to mitigate our concern about the tradeoff we're making for digital convenience 
in the past few years google facebook and other company that collect and keep gigantic trove of data about us have step up their effort to give us control over that data 
their primary argument is that user not the company are in charge of the whole game — we can affect what data is collected about us and how it's use 
that message doesn't seem to be get through 
large majority of america feel as we have little or no control over our search and purchase and browse history that our text and social media wandering are easily monitor and that even our physical location may be up for grab 
it get worse 
not only do we feel we have no control over our data but we're also sure there will be few consequence for misuse 
most america say they don't trust company to own up to mistake in the handle of our data or to suffer any serious punishment when things go wrong 
most of us say the companies' own privacy policy are meaningless 
not that this is a paranoid view 
if you consider recent history — say the fact that equifax was allow to stay in business after its gargantuan 2017 breach in which it fail at its one job collect and maintain americans' financial data — it stand to reason that punishment for wrongdoing will be light 
in july facebook was fine 5 billion by the federal trade commission for its role in the cambridge analytica privacy scandal — a fine that set a record but was of so little consequence to facebook's business that its stock price actually rose after the punishment was announce 
the pew survey show america are eager for more power over our data 
threequarter of respondent said there should be more regulation of what company can do with our data the view was share across the politics spectrum 
and america are wary of the fundamental tradeoff we're making for technology 
datahungry corporation insist that we're benefit from the surveillance state — and that our very acquiesce to the collection is a signal of our contentment 
in fact the vast majority of america say that the potential risk of data collection by company and the government outweigh the benefit 
but where do all this leave us 
ordinarily a finding of widespread discontent should spark a sense of optimism — if people hate the status quo so much and are beg for a new way forward won't the market or the government step in and give us something better 
but there is anothermore pessimist way to read this survey 
the tech company still enjoy enormous financial success and have seen little impact from increase scrutiny on their business 
this suggest none of it matter 
we hate the way things are but we've trade away our power to stop it and our worry won't change anything 
the prison is terrible 
we all know it 
enjoy your stay 
we made the coronaviru epidemic by david quammen jan 28 2020 the latest scary new virus that has capture the world's horrify attention cause a lockdown of 56 million people in china disrupt travel plan around the globe and spark a run on medical mask from wuhan hubei province to bryan texas is known provisional as ncov2019 
it's a clunky moniker for a lurid threat 
the name picked by the team of china scientist who isolated and identify the virus is short for novel coronaviru of 2019 
it reflect the fact that the virus was first recognize to have infect human late last year — in a seafood and liveanimal market in wuhan — and that it belong to the coronaviru family a notorious group 
the sar epidemic of 20023 which infect 8098 people worldwide killing 774 of them was cause by a coronaviru and so was the mer outbreak that began on the arabia peninsula in 2012 and still linger 2494 people infect and 858 death as of november 
despite the new virus's name though and as the people who christen it well know ncov2019 isn't as novel as you might think 
something very much like it was found several years ago in a cave in yunnan a province roughly a thousand mile southwest of wuhan by a team of perspicacious research who noted its existence with concern 
the fast spread of ncov2019 — more than 4500 confirmed case including at least 106 death as of tuesday morning and the figures will have risen by the time you read this — is startle but not unforeseeable 
that the virus emerge from a nonhuman animal probably a bat and possibly after passing through another creature may seem spooky yet it is utterly unsurprise to scientist who study these things 
one such scientist is zhengli shi of the wuhan institute of virology a senior author of the draft paper not yet peer review and so far available only in preprint that gave ncov2019 its identity and name 
it was ms shi and her collaborate who back in 2005 show that the sar pathogen was a bat virus that had spill over into people 
ms shi and colleague have been tracing coronaviruse in bats since then warning that some of them are unique suit to cause human pandemic 
in a 2017 paper they set out how after nearly five years of collect fecal sample from bats in the yunnan cave they had found coronaviruse in multiple individual of four different species of bats including one call the intermediate horseshoe bat because of the halfoval flap of skin protrude like a saucer around its nostril 
the genome of that virus ms shi and her colleague have now announce is 96 percent identical to the wuhan virus that has recently been found in human 
and those two constitute a pair distinct from all other known coronaviruse including the one that cause sar 
in this sense ncov2019 is novel — and possibly even more dangerous to human than the other coronaviruse 
i say possibly because so far not only do we not know how dangerous it is we can't know 
outbreak of new viral disease are like the steel balls in a pinball machine you can slap your flipper at them rock the machine on its leg and bonk the balls to the jittery ring but where they end up drop depend on 11 level of chance as well as on anything you do 
this is true with coronaviruse in particular they mutate often while they replicate and can evolve as quick as a nightmare ghoul 
peter daszak the president of ecohealth alliance a private research organization base in new york that focus on the connection between human and wildlife health is one of ms shi's longtime partner 
we've been raise the flag on these virus for 15 years he told me on friday with calm frustration 
ever since sar 
he was a coauthor of the 2005 batsandsar study and again of the 2017 paper about the multiple sarslike coronaviruse in the yunnan cave 
mr daszak told me that during that second study the field team took blood sample from a couple of thousand yunnanese people about 400 of whom live near the cave 
roughly 3 percent of them carry antibody against sarsrelate coronaviruse 
we don't know if they got sick 
we don't know if they were expose as children or adult mr daszak said 
but what it tell you is that these virus are making the jump repeatedly from bats to human 
in other words this wuhan emergency is no novel event 
it's part of a sequence of related contingency that stretch back into the past and will stretch forward into the future as long as current circumstances persist 
so when you're done worry about this outbreak worry about the next one 
or do something about the current circumstances 
current circumstances include a perilous trade in wildlife for food with supply chain stretch through asia africa and to a lesser extent the united states and elsewhere 
that trade has now been outlaw in china on a temporary basis but it was outlaw also during sar then allow to resume — with bats civet porcupine turtle bamboo rats many kind of bird and other animal pile together in market such as the one in wuhan 
current circumstances also include 76 billion hungry human some of them impoverish and desperate for protein some affluent and wasteful and empower to travel every which way by airplane 
these factor are unprecedented on planet earth we know from the fossil record by absence of evidence that no largebody animal has ever been nearly so abundant as human are now let alone so effective at arrogate resources 
and one consequence of that abundance that power and the consequent ecological disturbance is increase viral exchange — first from animal to human then from human to human sometimes on a pandemic scale 
we invade tropical forest and other wild landscape which harbor so many species of animal and plant — and within those creature so many unknown virus 
we cut the tree we kill the animal or cage them and send them to market 
we disrupt ecosystem and we shake virus loose from their natural host 
when that happen they need a new host 
often we are it 
the list of such virus emerge into human sound like a grim drumbeat machupo bolivia 1961 marburg germany 1967 ebola zaire and sudan 1976 hiv recognize in new york and california 1981 a form of hanta now known as sin nombre southwestern united states 1993 hendra australia 1994 bird flu hong kong 1997 nipah malaysia 1998 west nile new york 1999 sar china 20023 mer saudi arabia 2012 ebola again west africa 2014 
and that's just a selection 
now we have ncov2019 the latest thump on the drum 
current circumstances also include bureaucrat who lie and conceal bad news and elect official who brag to the crowd about cutting forest to create job in the timber industry and agriculture or about cutting budget for public health and research 
the distance from wuhan or the amazon to paris toronto or washington is short for some virus measured in hour given how well they can ride within airplane passenger 
and if you think fund pandemic preparedness is expensive wait until you see the final cost of ncov2019 
fortunately current circumstances also include brilliant dedicated scientist and outbreakresponse medical people — such as many at the wuhan institute of virology ecohealth alliance the united states center for disease control and prevention cdc 
the china cdc 
and numerous other institution 
these are the people who go into bat cave swamp and highsecur containment laboratory often risk their lives to bring out bat feces and blood and other precious evidence to study genomic sequence and answer the key question 
as the number of ncov2019 case has increase and the death toll along with it one metric the case fatality rate has remain rather steady so far at about or below 3 percent 
as of tuesday less than three out of 100 confirmed case had die 
that's relatively good luck — worse than for most strain of influenza better than for sar 
this good luck may not last 
nobody know where the pinball will go 
four days from today the number of case may be in the ten of thousand 
six month from today wuhan pneumonia may be recede into memory 
or not 
we are face with two mortal challenge in the short term and the long term 
short term we must do everything we can with intelligence calm and a full commitment of resources to contain and extinguish this ncov2019 outbreak before it become as it could a devastating global pandemic 
long term we must remember when the dust settle that ncov2019 was not a novel event or a misfortune that befell us 
it was — it is — part of a pattern of choice that we human are making 
we really must stop start war by farhad manjoo jan 9 2020 let us not go again to war 
let us not go to war because we cannot afford to win another war 
there would be no winning this war 
there is only lose at a cost that staggers every dimension on all side — in lives in money and in the squander opportunity to do anything better with our collective time and resources on this already beset planet 
i'm speak here of war with iran our current precipice 
but i issue the warning more generally too 
bookmark this page and pull it up as prophylaxis anytime the drum of war begin rattling anew war isn't just tragic 
it is increasingly dumb and pointless too 
war is becoming an outdated means of human conflict resolution 
technology is turning armed conflict into an endeavor increasingly dominate by what war scholar call asymmetric warfare — meaning that weak powers like iran can now marshal so much strength that they are no long very weak exacting a mighty cost of victory even to the world's preeminent global superpower 
then there is climate change which has ratchet up the opportunity cost of every conflict anytime we are fight each other we are abscond in the large and more important fight for the habitable of the planet 
you may debate whether any particular historical war work out well for its agitator 
but there should be no debate that many of america's recent war have end in misery for all 
our politician talk of war as a last resort but that is only to keep up appearances because the truth is too terrible to admit that our evermoreexpensive war machine a cost of nearly 740 billion in 2020 can buy us little peace 
rather than a last resort war now offer no resort 
war can no long be defend as the thing to do after everything else has fail 
war must instead be seen as failure itself 
i had thought the futility of war might be grasp by most america politician by now 
one of donald trump's rare bright spot as a candidate was his departure from the post911 bushcheney doctrine that double down on heedless america military intervention 
in his oftstate aversion to endless war trump's sentiment match the public's — a pew poll this summer show that most america including most military veteran now believe that our war in afghanistan and iraq have not been worth fight 
trump seem to be heed the public's caution back in the summer when he abrupt call off a strike against iran in retaliation for its shoot down an america surveillance drone 
but in killing iran's most important military leader maj gen qassim suleimani trump open the door to war 
now iran is retaliate and a cycle of escalate looks possible — even if for now trump is backing away from further conflict 
it's beginning to feel a lot like 2003 again with some of the same pundit and politician who were in favor of a war with iraq now repeating similar talk points about iran 
while note that he'd like to avoid war trump himself has suggest that war with iran would be a cakewalk it wouldn't last very long i can tell you that the president told fox business in june 
don't fall for it 
it's plain dishonesty how could anyone who has live through the quagmire of iraq and afghanistan think war with iran will be anything but long and brutal 
in those conflict america's overwhelming military might stumble on local culture geography ethnic and religious rivalry and most of all the determination of an entrenched committed foe that could melt in and out of the local population 
as vox's alex ward points out iran has almost three times as many people as iraq did when we invade in 2003 
it also has treacherous geography and it control a great many proxy forces across the middle east and even in likely sleeper cell in europe and latin america 
iran also possess a sophisticated cyberwar operation — it is believe to be behind recent hack into america bank and other target and to have spread disinformation and propaganda on social network around the world 
the united states would overwhelm iran in a conventional headon war but like china and russia iran has adopt a deep capacity to mount hybrid war — conflict that involve both conventional and unconventional means of war 
for example iran could expand its operation on oil tanker in the strait of hormuz dealing a costly rise in global energy price 
as ward conclude a usiran war would be a bloody hell during and after the fight 
this get to the immense folly at the heart of our military might 
though the united states spend more on the military than the next nine country combine we have not been able to purchase much peace through strength 
that's because our strength is clearly of a type and our years in iraq and afghanistan have made plain our vulnerable 
among other shortcoming our military is still buy mostly big old defense technology like aircraft carrier and bomber from the militaryindustrial complex even if many of these technology face obsolescence under a future of artificial intelligence unmann battlefield robot and other cyberweapon 
our country's effort at adopt artificial intelligence technology in the military might not be enough to counter our rival including russia and china 
the upshot is this the united states hold military supremacy over the world's waters and the airspace but our control is limited and contest 
the last two decade have made clear that even for america war is never simple 
we should fear it 
we should avoid it 
and we ought to look for more fruitful things to do with our money and our lives like making life on earth more livable not less 
what do it mean to have a serious drink problem 
by nance wartik jan 31 2020 one day in the fall of 2018 i woke up feeling wreck 
the night before i'd had beer with colleague and wound up bray loud to one of them about something she'd confide and what i thought she should do 
i wish i'd never told you this she finally blurt and i knew i'd betray a trust 
a few nights before i'd been more inept 
a group of us had held a memorial for a friend 
at a gathering later i'd had a martini with prosecco chaser then picked a senseless quarrel with our hostess a close friend as bereaved as i was 
now i sat there head pounding stomach roile 
it was another in a string of mornings when i'd woken wanting to smother myself with a pillow 
booze it didn't take much for me to feel the effects 
alcohol could make nights glittery and fun make me love all humankind 
it could also and unpredictable rouse demon that turn me into a wifely shrew spark bruising argument unleash embarrass faux pas 
this morning a new thought struck penetrating to the bone 
i can't do it anymore 
i quit 
although i'd grapple for decade with my relationship to alcohol i didn't consider myself an alcoholic 
in online quizze ask how many drink i typically had per day i could fairly accurate answer two very generous drink 
on the world health organization's audit quiz which test for drink problem i score eight of 40 points making me a medium drinker with a risky pattern 
but medium didn't sound too bad and the website said i could alter my drink without too much difficulty 
plus i had the vaunt female triumvirate husband kid respectable job 
friends when they weren't mad at me 
ok sometimes i overdid it 
but it was easy to imagine myself as your average funlove parisian oenophile 
and yet 
i was in my late teens when i discover what alcohol could do quash my inhibition kindle false intimacy provoke brilliant revelation that i soon forgot 
alcohol made me the outgoing person my unconfident self want to be let me talk to people i normally wouldn't have 
yes occasional i awoke to see a head on the adjoin pillow and felt a bolt of regret 
damn 
why did this guy seem cute last night 
but i'd call a friend guess what i did this time 
i'd ask turning discomfort into a hilarious anecdote 
or a friend would inform me of my revelry nance the bartender threw you out 
you couldn't stay on your stool 
alcohol was also medication 
i drank to quiet angst or because i was lonesome 
i drank it took years to realize because i had clinical depression 
eventually i treat the depression but kept drink 
alcohol was my stress reduce my reality fighter the confer of artificial joy 
life change in my 40s 
i married and with my husband adopt our beloved daughter now 17 
working from home i made dinner drink wine with a neighbor mom 
my morningafter headache were worsen though 
nights rather than reading or chat with my husband i'd crash 
i fear my drink was destroy brain cell 
i'd written about how alcohol is hard on women than men and that worried me too 
some years ago to prove i had control i cut down to five nights a week 
it was tough 
how could i not drink after a rough day 
i couldn't manage two consecutive sober nights 
achieve my two sober nights was always an exercise in militarylevel strategize 
but every sunday i felt virtuous 
an actual alcoholic couldn't skip any nights i thought 
but i could 
what do it mean to have a serious drink problem 
the answer is surprising vague 
alcoholism isn't an actual diagnosis 
in 1980 the america psychiatric association's authoritative diagnostic and statistic manual of mental disorder establish two different classification alcohol abuse and alcohol dependence 
in 2013 the dsm 
combine the category to create alcohol use disorder a spectrum range from mild to severe base not on how much someone drink but on how many of 11 behavior or psychological symptom a person has 
meanwhile the center for disease control and prevention has its own standard focus more on quantity of alcoholic consumption 
seven drink per week or few is considered safe for women 14 or few for men 
but guidelines fluctuate international according to a stanford university study from 2016 
in canada or france you can drink more weekly and be considered low risk 
moreover a recent study in the lancet conclude alcohol is so tough on health that there's no safe level 
in short if you wonder whether you drink too much sometimes it's best to trust your gut 
i don't know exactly what happen that fall morning as i sat in bed achy and humiliate 
as visceral as i've known anything i knew i was in trouble 
so what if i didn't swig a bottle of scotch daily 
i'd hit medium drinker rock bottom and it was enough 
despite the website saying i could change my drink without too much difficulty quit booze is one of the hardest things i've ever done 
i pine for it at restaurant i'd gaze at ruby goblet as if at a divine elixir 
after workout i'd crave a beer 
and what was the point of socialize sober 
eventually i had to try 
guzzle nonalcoholic beer — before i wise switch to seltzer — while chat with people savor complex pinot noir was initially daunt 
but astonishing my nonintoxicate brain still found what they said funny touching or interesting 
i didn't join aa though i don't rule it out 
i sought support from my husband daughter and friends — those i'd offend those surprise i even had a problem 
i devour others' story watch movies about alcoholic reading memoirs lurk in subreddit for people struggle to quit 
but what really kept me on the path was the remarkable difference between the drink and not drink me 
i hadn't grasp the degree to which a sense of shame had insidious undergirded my life 
now it was gone replace by an unaccustomed pride 
the long i abstain the better i felt in ways that spill into marriage work parent friendship 
recently someone unaware i'd quit told me i look years younger 
i'm more patient 
my headache are infrequent my energy up 
those result fit with a study publish in the canada medical association journal among the first focus on moderate drinkers' mental health 
research study cohort of people in hong kong and the united states found even safe drinker women in particular show improve wellbeing if they stop 
today i can label myself 
i had moderate alcohol use disorder a chronic relapse brain disease marked by loss of control over alcohol 
the national institute on alcoholism and alcohol abuse say 62 percent of america adult more than 15 million people are on the alcohol use disorder spectrum 
other research put the numbers higher 
i'd guess many like me drink modest enough that they don't believe they have a problem 
i feel lucky i quit before anything worse happen 
sobriety can still be a challenge 
if all go according to plan i'll never again experience the soft scrim that drops between me and reality as wine drain from my glass 
it seem sad until i remember that three times since quit i've try a celebratory drink 
most recently in peru i had one of the country's famous pisco sour 
it gave me a mild buzz and a hangover 
i haven't had a drop since 
these days i awaken clearheade 
i'm close than ever to being the mother wife relative and friend i want to be 
it feel good 
really good 
i get up the next morning 
i do it again

the first approach as sunstein put it is this suppose that a president engage in certain action that seem to you very very bad

in short trump's plan almost succeed — and in any case he will get away with it in the sense that he is sure to be acquit by the senate 
when republican suggest that trump did nothing wrong what message do that impunity send to trump and to future president 
the third thought experiment is simple what if trump weren't president but was like almost any other person in america

the favor would be an investigate of the vice principal's exwife before their upcoming child custody hearing in hope of tilt the outcome in his favor 
in that situation the vice principal would be fire 
we all recognize that no school official or other person in a government bureaucracy should use public power for private benefit 
so a last query shouldn't we have as high a standard for the president of the united states as for a school vice principal

by charlie warzel jan 29 2020 the culture war will come for us all

for newsroom leader the question get tough fast 
few if any outlet seem to want to draw exact lines

and in a volatile industry it get you notice 
being part of the discourse each day means being market 
it help writer but it also bolster publication helping promote big story and create all kind of dystopian form of content like microscoop or break news too small to merit its own article but enough to tout to competitor on twitter 
this exposure is a drug for journalist 
the realtime spar and feedback is seductive and the endorphin boost of constant mention is addictive 
but it's also exposure in the truest sense great visibility and great vulnerable blend seamless together 
though an argument could be made that all the timewast injoke and gaffe from idle reporter and editor on twitter subtle undermine the rigorous parts of the work newsroom benefit greatly from the constant exposure of their journalist 
reporter use twitter to poke and prod source 
writer sometimes enhance their story with long tweet thread that explain the report process 
and reporter build trust with audience by including or signal to their audience perspective in their online analysis ms sonmez who has come forward with detail of her own sexual assault told her colleague erik wemple that her tweet were in part to make survivor like herself who follow her feel seen 
when important news break newsroom claim credit when their reporter break it first on twitter 
which is why the post's statement especially its urge of restraint is so fraught 
the same editor who want restraint from reporter online during a celebrity death would most likely also be furious if their capitol hill reporter were slow in livetweete a hearing or impeach proceeding and fell behind the competition 
restraint is a virtue in journalism no doubt but so are tenacity and transparency 
the message is contradictory broadcast everything but exercise restraint 
twitter isn't real life but tweet can and will get you fire or suspend 
but these quality have been in conflict and competition for long before twitter and newsroom understood a journalist exposure during break news and had their back accordingly 
evidence suggest that's not always the case in the face of a cascade of online outrage 
that's less a change in the industry than it is a failure of newsroom leader to understand the information war it send its journalist out to fight in each day 
while the internet's culture war dynamics are fraught they're not all that hard to understand 
they come in the form of intimidation and threat toward journalist and angry campaign toward advertise and executive 
some of the response are posture and some are real but all are engineer for maximum viral and outrage 
yes sometimes journalist make mistake 
sometimes work will harm the institution or undermine coworker but newsroom leader ought to be train to distinguish troll from goodfaith criticism 
it's a weird moment that newsroom aren't talk about enough 
just as social media platform allow celebrity politician and influence to circumvent traditional press gatekeepe the same thing has happen to journalism's own practitioner 
despite all the social media guidelines there's an unanswered question who do those follower really belong to 
perhaps it's most accurate to say they're an asset and a liability for both party 
everyone's expose 
but there's an asymmetry to that exposure 
the culture war will come for us all institution and individual alike 
one group can weather the storm the other needs protection 
newsroom need to get smart prepare and protect their foot soldier 
it's the least they can do

why trump persist by thomas b edsall jan 22 2020 the failure of the america electorate to rise up in opposition to president trump — whose outrage are welldocumente — suggest that voter are less tolerant less empathetic and less insistent on integrity than many believe 
the election of trump and his first three years in office have reveal a nation deep ambivalent about immigrate race equality fair — even about the ground rule of democracy itself 
what if the belief system use to justify antiimmigrant policy and to justify race prejudice for that matter — hostility to outsider insularity high sensitivity to external threat — are as deep ingrained in the america body politic as belief system sympathetic to immigrate and to racial equality — open receptive to new experience trust 
karen stenner a politics psychologist and behavior economist best known for predict the rise of trumplike figures under the kind of conditions we now confront respond to my emaile inquiry by note the conflict pressure at play i don't think i would agree that trumpian conservative stand on immigrate race and homeless are a more natural or default position 
community with a good balance of people who seek out diversity complexity novelty new and exciting experience etc and those who are disgust by and averse to such things avoid them and tell other to do likewise tend to thrive and prosper in human evolution 
finding the right balance stenner said is vital to both societal cohesion and human flourish 
but she warn we may have tip the balance too far in favor of unconstrained diversity and complexity push the boundary beyond many people's capacity to tolerate it 
at this juncture she argue we need to tinker with that balance and get it right for everyone 
so there's the paradox of our times it is likely that rather less liberal democracy will ultimately make liberal democracy more secure 
among liberal stenner argue the greatest ambivalence attach to immigrate issue and that ambivalence is only worsen by the unwilling of liberal to accept an open debate in which immigrate opponent can express their fear and concern without being call racist 
suzette brook master — who has written extensive about immigrant integrate detention employmentbase immigrate and the immigrants' rights field generally — made a parallel point in her recent study of immigrate change is hard academic agree that it is the pace of change relative to the composition of the receiving community that matter most 
simply put if a place is already quite diverse making it more diverse matter less 
even significant inflow of diverse newcomer will be perceive as less threaten because the community has already adapt to greater diversity 
by contrast in a relatively homogeneous location even small absolute numbers of newcomer such as refugee can be disrupt and activate cultural anxiety 
jonathan haidt a professor at nyu's stern school of business offer a similarly nuance examination of how the balance between tribalism and open might play out 
tribalism he wrote by email is not a mindless and eternal us versus them mentality 
it is a set of psychological adaptation that make people respond to threat and intergroup competition with an urge to band together enforce loyalty to the team and guard boundary or territory 
in the politics arena haidt continue if one gain prestige for outdo other on one's devotion to sacred value — such as guard america's border on the right or being antiracist on the left — then the party's rhetoric will shift to the extreme with candidate making more extreme proposal that gain them prestige 
the pressure to go to extreme haidt suggest are roughly symmetrical between left and right 
john r hibb a politics scientist at the university of nebraska take a more uncompromising stance 
in an email he wrote though consideration of such matter is always speculative suggest the possibility that conservative orientation particularly on topic such as immigrate and race are evolutionary more primal is perfectly reasonable 
in their book predispose liberal conservative and the biology of politics difference hibb kevin b smith of the university of nebraska and john r alford of rice argue that liberalism is an evolutionary luxury that can emerge in people when negative stimuli becoming less prevalent and less deadly or as hibb put it in an email when daily threat to life and limb pose by other human being have diminish 
converse they write if the environment shift back to a threatfill atmosphere then positive selection for conservative orientation would reappear 
let's take a look at one of the core division between liberal and conservative the cause of poverty 
the right tend to blame individual failing while the left tend to place the onus on economic and politics forces 
the accompany chart create from 2019 voter study group data by zach goldberg a doctoral candidate in politics science at georgia state show the difference 
linda j skitka a professor of psychology at the university of illinois at chicago and four colleague conduct an intrigue set of test to determine the durable and strength of liberal and conservative belief on poverty in a 2002 paper disposition script or motivate correction 
understanding ideology difference in explanation for social problem 
they found that in trouble times when competition for limited goods intensify liberal move to the right it is much easy to get a liberal to behave like a conservative than it is to get a conservative to behave like a liberal 
liberal act like conservative when resources are scarce cognitive load is high and aid serve secondary rather than primary needs 
conservative only act like liberal when they are ask to consider helping a person with internal control cause of need who has convincing reform 
in an email skitka provided some reason for this difference my research has found that holding people responsible for their plight is a more natural response than feeling sympathetic to those in need 
under most conditions liberal are more sympathetic to the needy in large part because they are more likely to attribute the cause of their need to something about the situation 
conservative in contrast tend to attribute the cause of people's need to something about the needy person they don't work hard enough etc 
because blame the individual is a default or fallback position liberal have to go through a more cognitive effortful process to reach their less natural conclusion — people have to basically override a more natural inclination to make disposition attribution instead according to skitka 
as a result she continue under certain pressure liberal respond to the needy more like conservative when resources are scarce or when they are under a lot of cognitive load eg they are distracted or their ability to engage in selfcontrol is reduce eg when under the influence of alcohol 
the leftright difference over the cause of poverty apply to other controversial subject highly salient in contemporary america politics skitka and her colleague write liberal tend to focus on situation or institution explanation for things like homeless or why people commit crime whereas conservative tend to focus on personal explanation for the same phenomena 
skitka and her fellow author received strong support for their argument in a 2012 paper loweffort thought promote politics conservatism by scott eidelman a professor of psychology at the university of arkansas and three coauthor 
eidelman and his colleague conduct a series of test compare the answer of two group to ideology revealing question 
the first face time pressure or were forced to answer with distract background noise in environment tax limiting or otherwise disengage effortful deliberative thought 
the second group was ask the same question with plenty of time to think and without noise or other distraction 
in each case those test under favorable circumstances provided more liberal answer than those test under more hostile conditions 
the adverse conditions forced those participant to perform what the author call loweffort thinking and the result show that loweffort thinking promote politics conservatism 
in one of their four experiment the author went to an unidentified bar in new england and persuade 85 drinker to take the test and have their alcohol level measured 
the result bar patron report more conservative attitude as their level of alcohol intoxicate increase 
because alcohol limit cognitive capacity and disrupt control respond while leave automatic thinking largely intact these data are consistent with our claim that loweffort thinking promote politics conservatism 
diana mutz a professor of politics science and communication at the university of pennsylvania pointed out that one effect of increase education level is to fundamentally change individual world view 
the one sense in which there is evidence that we do 'overcome' our tendency toward tribalism is through education she wrote by email 
every study i've ever seen across the social science show that education promote less ingroup favoritism and greater tolerance toward those unlike ourselves she continue 
in panel study that track the same people over time as people gain advanced level of education they become more tolerant and favorable toward liberal democratic norm 
one scholar who has devoted much of his career to the study of the transition in develop country from materialist to postmaterialist value — from a value orientation that emphasize economic and physical security to one that emphasize selfexpression and quality of life — is ronald inglehart a professor of politics science at the university of michigan 
he see a generalize transition to more liberal world view — perhaps as a concomitant of voter with college and graduate school degree 
liberal value are not a veneer mask a much less pleasant reality inglehart pointed out in an email

brexit has arrive 
but boris johnson's reign is just beginning 
by richard seymour jan 31 2020 london — the moment has arrive 
britain is out of the europe union 
prime minister boris johnson and his people's government — it scarcely call itself conservative at this point — has fulfill the promise on which it was elect in december and got brexit done 
there are difficulty ahead 
mr johnson has promise impossible and contradictory things on brexit maximum regulatory freedom where it suit his government maximum frictionless trade where it suit the britain economy 
the europe union is unlikely to give him what he wants in the month of negotiation to come 
but by fulfill his pledge mr johnson has won enormous good will from nationalist voter across england and wales 
outside the europe union he will also have more scope to change the britain government's role in the economy 
this give him a unique opportunity do what his predecessor could not build a lasting popular base for the conservative party 
mr johnson can now take advantage of his big majority to overhaul britain capitalism incentive longterm conservative voter while permanent annexe chunk of the labour party's historic base 
already the dimensions of mr johnson's plan are becoming clear 
he has no intention of running the country as any conservative leader since margaret thatch would have he is not out to roll back the state 
instead he is out to secure the support of workingclass voter who hand over to the tory dozen of seat formerly held by labour 
his premiership set free by brexit could reshape britain's electoral map for decade 
during the election mr johnson campaign as an almost singleissue nationalist the phrase get brexit done fall robot from his lip between every other stammer 
beyond that much of what he said was conventional tory he promise harsh restriction on immigrate meaning an end to free movement from the europe union and the expansion of the hostile environment for migrant 
domestic repression the manifesto promise would also tighten with a big penal system and a greater emphasis on counterextrem which as home secretary priti patel has indicate will target parts of the left 
mr johnson has also hint at constitutional reform which would strengthen the executive and weaken judicial challenge 
he promise an attack on liberal norm and legality in the name of national invigorate 
telling he distance himself from the last government 
he would end austerity raise spend on the national health service guarantee pension raise the minimum wage and borrow �100 billion to invest in infrastructure 
many of these promise were gross exaggerate but they serve to underline the point that a johnson administration would be different 
and since the election the government has act to carry out its commitment passing legislation to guarantee nhs 
spend increase and propose moderate improvement to workers' and renters' rights 
it has also promise that most of the infrastructure spend will be invest in england's deprived northern regions — and this week back up the promise by nationalize the north's major rail service 
if this sound like an incursion into labour territory it is 
many of the policy are directly taken from labour's plan 
the push for a large state resonate with a politics ambiguous popular memory of the postwar era — a certain nostalgia for the era of big dynamic industry own by the britain government inflect both a version of the leftw politics of the labour party leader jeremy corbyn and a version of brexit sentiment 
mr johnson know that many of the vote contribute to a conservative majority were lent by voter who want brexit done 
a more interventionist state is a way to shore up a lasting broad coalition 
this pragmatic raid on enemy turf was first conceive under mr johnson's predecessor theresa may 
more thoughtful tory knew they had to change 
the britain state and economy had become dysfunctional gape regional inequality a housing market inaccessible to younger worker weak labor productivity sluggish investment and very little to export 
mrs may's adviser understood that the conservative had to break with the formula of austerity and financial somehow 
but while she use the rhetoric of workingclass uplift she was unable to back it up with policy 
her chancellor philip hammond a traditional ally of the bank was determined to keep austerity go 
if nothing else he could see no other way to create a fiscal surplus big enough to soften the impact of brexit 
mr johnson by contrast is just enough of an opportunist to see that deliver brexit in however selfinjure and punitive a form give him both the politics power and the regulatory latitude to do things different 
there is a risk though of succumb to mr johnson's own mythmake 
as much as he needs workingclass conservative they have always exist 
and the core tory voter remains the affluent middle class 
what's more when it come to public spend he's limited in what he can do by his commitment to freezing most tax 
in an economy that is already weak and likely to be weak after brexit he has little room for serious investment 
and mr johnson will face conflict demand from within his own party 
the chancellor sajid javid has demand 5 percent cut from most government department making plain that the spend spigot are not about to freely flow 
and the prime minister is surround by ally who far from wanting a more interventionist state want to cut tax and slash regulation in the interests of a more global competitive economy 
during the election mr johnson was able to glide over the glaring contradiction in what he said with a bustle con man's charm but in office he has to navigate them 
with a big majority he can no long play the outsider 
however the lesson of nationalist leader global is that in this jittery era they don't have to deliver boom success to keep power 
from viktor orban in hungary to narendra modi in india these leader have expand their base by deliver a personalize charismatic form of rule in which they are militant defend of the nation against all comer — be they foreigner traitor liberal or leftist 
mr johnson is not a nationalist by conviction 
he is the epitome of the reckless opportunist that as the sociologist aeron davis say run britain 
his vote record in parliament show him to be slightly more liberal than his party 
but his performance over the last few month — during which he agitate against parliament accused opponent of collaboration with europe and saberrattle against the court and media — show him to be adept at use the far right's template 
whenever the contradiction in his government threaten to unravel he is likely to return to these tactics 
indeed brexit fit in with that method perfectly 
after today mr johnson will be able to continual remind voter that he was able to overcome the hostility of the liberal elite and accomplish his goal 
and as negotiation proceed he can gin up hostility against his supposed enemy whenever he doesn't get his way 
whenever any politician claim to speak for the people someone always pay the price 
migrant are first on the list for mr johnson 
but they will not be the last
